Elden ring combines the best mechanics from previous souls games with new mechanics such as jumping, horse riding, and summoning. Great video! I played the network test as well and wanted to mention one thing that was not said about ashes of war. Maybe this is already known, but when you are using an ash of war that combos (for example the thunderbolt ash of war or storm blade), you can overcast the combo with no mana as long as you have stamina to spend. So in order to maximize your mana if you cast your final ash of war with a full stamina bar you can chain that ash of war for no mana cost as many times as you want as long as you have stamina to spend!

I don't like the jumping in realistic games. Some people say that jumping in ER will increase the exploration. I debunk: 1- If you hike in mountains there are places IMPOSSIBLE to reach by humanly jumping, forcing you to EXPLORE for a possible safe route. 2- Barely falling damage makes EASY to just jump off most cliffs to get down. But when theres realistic falling damage, you have to think how to get down safely.  ER should have introduced climbing and ropes/ladder items, and humanly possible jumps. That would have make exploration more puzzle like, and keep realistic movements.

Those small details you mentioned earlier really sets games apart for me. Like a character or vehicle being underwater having little air bubbles, such a small thing to include, but makes the game more immersive. Something being diegetic means it is occurring within the context of the story and can be heard by the characters, not seen. So unless that guiding light makes some sort of sound that indicates the direction that the player should move in, it doesn't seem accurate to call it diegetic. So one downside is the backstab changes for PVP.  Essentially it's the DS3 system, plus a more restrictive angle check.  So when your backstab goes to your opponent and gets checked, they have to be 1.5m from you, and you have to be within 30 degrees of directly behind them (ie, a 60 degree cone).  This is SIGNIFICANTLY more restrictive than DS3 backstabs and means that basically you can only backstab someone if they are pretty much completely stationary the whole time.  Even worse, you still have the "whiffed backstab" animation, which is REAL rough because of the angle restrictions basically any fast weapon user who is spamming R1 while locked on will literally just automatically turn, force your backstab to whiff, and then they'll be hitting you while you do the "whiff backstab" animation.    This means in PVP, backstabs are mostly useless except against the longest, most easily punished animations.  In fact, in most cases they are WORSE than useless - you will literally eat extra hits for trying to backstab someone. Hopefully they get a happy medium back because currently you want to basically avoid backstabbing if at all possible.  The only real issue with DS3 backstabs was they were too good and too easy against ultra weapons which kind of invalidated a whole class of cool weapons. The only real benefit of the Elden Ring backstab changes is that it should pretty much eliminate "facestabs"... but facestabs were almost entirely avoidable in DS3 anyways if you just moved instead of trying to turn.  Now turning to face your would-be backstabber is basically a guarantee that their backstab will whiff.
Think I'll wait for a actual review rather then a shill.

I know my comment will get lost in a sea of comments, but I'll make it anyways... First and foremost I admit I've never played a From Software game and at the same time every single time I see someone talk about them or even the company talk about them I get annoyed. I fully do not agree with the philosophy of, "die a million times as a trial and error" way of playing. There's only so many game overs I can get in a game before I literally have no more fun and any sense of, "accomplishment" the developers intended is long destroyed and I move on to a better game. Fans of From Software, I swear, can be some of the harshest and angriest crowd I've ever seen, saying you don't like Dark Souls or Bloodborne throws them into a tirade of Internet insults and tidal waves of, "scrub" "git gud" and other extremely non-helpful and very un-sportsman like insults.  Then there's their stories. I'm not gonna claim I've done a lot of reading on their series' stories, but from what I understand (and could be wrong) their stories are purposefully underdeveloped in order to let the player kinda piece things together or make up things as they go... Personally to me that makes it feel like they just were either lazy or didn't care enough to write a good narrative, so again that goes against what I like in games.  With a game that is supposed to be notoriously difficult with a vague plot at best, why am I still watching videos on Elden Ring? It isn't because GRRM is involved, I have a strong feeling his involvement at best was limited to only creating a backdrop (and the utter disappointment of the ending of Game of Thrones as well as his seemingly lack of interest in completing his own epic has convinced me he is way more into just living out his life with the money he has acquired rather than complete what he started)... But this game DOES just look like a huge Dark Souls game. I can only imagine it'll come out, fanboys will lap it up and call it delicious and it'll probably win Game of the Year 2022 because, "it's expected to win".  I actually kinda do want to play this game, but I have a strong feeling I'd get maybe a few hours in and just delete it and feel I wasted money... Whilst again I admit I haven't played any Souls games, I've played the infamous "souls-like" games before even knowing that was a genre. Nioh and Code Vein I wanted to get into, but quickly realised that they aren't my style. The controls in particular feel incredibly weak and "floatly" and even watching Souls videos I say aloud to myself, "then why bother having a health bar when one attack just sinks your health to zero?"   I probably won't play it, but at least it piqued my curiosity. I just cannot give money to a company I feel purposefully makes its games difficult just for the sake of doing it. I play games to escape my life and if I get better along the way, great! But just dropping a player into a world and saying, "hope for the best!" with crazy difficultly? Nah, I'd rather spend my money elsewhere.

I appreciate the fact that as a solo-player you can't be invaded unless you want to (using that one item), because random invasions have always been something I disliked in games when I am playing solo. One feels that the ideas have dried up. And open world's  like that was made 10 years ago in some seedy Assassin's Creed or Dragon's Dogma. We loved the first part for its ingenious complexity. The style was consistent - pure dark fantasy. Antique and biblical proportion. No weapon was useless - we went to Gwyn with the Balder Side Sword. Eeverything was in place and new. In the world felt mystery at all levels. And now in this game the endless retextures, animations reuse, impotence of ideas and design. Earlier it was still possible to reconcile. But in 2022 it's already nauseous. I see that everything was as follows: - Mr. Miyazaki-san invented basic concept and the main dramatic conflict. - A covid hit the world. - There is nowhere to go - everything has already been signed up for investors and publishers' PR managers. - In a hurry, they piled old content into the field and everything that was in the archives. - In the end, everything just turned into a comedy. What worries me about the open-world nature of this game is that it inherently kills much of the tension that previous soulsborne games had. In previous titles, to progress through the level you'd HAVE TO confront that giant knight in the dimly lit hallway, or you'd HAVE TO fight that npc invader lurking along the tight path.  With open-world and a fast steed, it looks like you can just run away from any encounter you don't want to do (above ground).  Don't get me wrong, the game looks amazing and it would've been a shame if FromSoft did the same exact level design again, but there's something lost in the physical freedom the player now has.  The constant, oppressive threat of getting murderered in a dingy alley is sacrificed for mobility and freedom.

Game of the year
It's as I usually say: From Software keeps remaking the same game, over and over again, just with different maps/stories and a refining of existing mechanics, as well as adding new ones.  I usually say that Dark Souls 3 and Bloodborne are basically the epitome of what started as a first person RPG game (King's Field), then transitioned into 3rd person (Demon's Souls) and continued the same path. Reused enemies and items from previous games (Seath and Moonlight Sword for example) are just examples of that, literalized. But the core is always the same: satisfying tactical combat with a huge emphasis on "dodge/block and hit". They aren't doing anything new.  HOWEVER... They keep refining. Adding new stuff. And what was once a dated formula, now becomes more and more intrincate and a monster of its own. Elden Ring, as you said, seems to be the result of every past work of theirs. It's familiar yet different.  Which is why "soulslike" games will always fall short. Only FromSoft can make Souls games. And Souls games can be summed up as challenging and very immersive action RPGs with emphasis on lore rather than story.  With that said... I am happy to hear that the open world isn't just an "open space", but an actual WORLD. And I am also happy to see the freedom available to you as a player with the horse riding. I imagine it won't feel tiring to wander through the world if we're going fast.  I was going to give up Souls games as they felt more and more repetitive. Seems like FromSoft anticipated it. I will definitely be playing this!  EDIT: wait, we can respawn near bosses now?! OH MAH GAWD THEY LISTENED

So, the one thing I feel in love with from the Souls games, was the level design in DS1. Having all those little shortcuts connecting the different areas, being able to access a whole bunch of them if you go off the "intended" path right from the start etc. It was pretty much the main thing I missed in DS3, at least to the extent of DS1. Admittedly, I didn't even end up looking at the Ashes of Andariel DLC, so maybe I'm not giving the game enough justice. But from what I've seen so far, as well as descriptions in other gameplay videos, it doesn't sound like this game will go back to that kind of level design. Based on the mention of Elden Rings level design being a sort of culmination what FromSoftware did and learned in their other games, it does get my hopes up a bit. The online really doesn't make a lot of sense. For starters, there are going to be so few people that want to consume not one, but TWO items to be solo invaded... and secondly, non shared progression in Co OP in an open world game just doesn't make any sense. The game is supposed to be about exploration and going in random directions, this would be great to do with a partner, but doing it for a second time in your own world is just going to feel like a drag after you just did it. It's fine in Dark Souls because the levels are more closed in, you know which section comes up next.  So what this results in, is: People will summon others just for bosses. Meaning as an invader who can only invade co op sessions... you will be invading people JUST about to start a boss, almost every time. I see this as being true because who, as they sit there watching this is thinking "My first playthrough is gonna be co op" doing it with a friend, then by yourself, for every single section of this OPEN world game. The design just doesn't make sense to me at all.

I regret doing that.  3:15 Are there quicker alternatives to the counter? Because if you're always forced to have a substantial gap after blocking, attacking a blocking opponent will usually be safe if they don't parry and the attacker gets the timing down.  Is there any incentive to do running attacks over jumping attacks? I presume jumping attacks are immune to parrying, which are the main problem with doing running attacks.  Shortbows were toxic in DS3 pvp. Will we see that again with quick bow attacks?  Charging spells was always needed, but can also make some spells toxic (e.g. lightning bow).  16:28 Does freeaiming spells only use the camera for the vertical inclination again?  21:25 This does well to rebalance ganking, but if the invader is already getting ganked, it means that the core pvp just isn't working for either side. On a personal note, I will never stop fighting against the notion that any empty space in an open world game is inherently a bad thing. Pacing and "room to breath" between packed areas are precisely two things an open world needs. If anything the real enemy is generic sameness across the board for the sake of filling the map.

This comment is only about the PVP stat balance and perhaps stats for the whole game. Based on previous games and what I have seen so far, and still early to tell especially since we don't know how the matchmaking will be, but I feel STR builds will be busted. DEX seems like once again just inferior to STR as at only gets "reduced fall damage" which has always been useless, and STR has always had all the shield options tied to it alongside the weight being an extra factor to use shields. And at least in previous games, DEX and everything else missed out on 2 handed bonus scaling benefits that STR had.  And spell builds always required an insane investment to even try be remotely evenly matched to a pure melee build in a 1vs1 especially with heals involved, and easy to avoid spells until the caster runs out of FP and has next to no heals due to the HP/FP heal split that have to go for and the innate squishiness due to being a caster build.  But now STR has equip weight built in so 1 stat they can completely ignore that previous games had to level up. Also Stamina cost seems to be messed up now on attacks and again for rolling, once again Roll Souls 3-like again. But once again this also means an additional stat STR builds can ignore, that is based on the stamina consumption I seen so far and I can't imagine another weapon actually requiring an investment in Stamina.  And now with poise the STR builds can have the best armor by default and always win trades and do big damage all in a single stat? This doesn't seem right. Especially if they can do something like R1 spam on a fast weapon with a STR infusion using the Ashes of War and become unstoppable traders. Then even if I have a light build and a fast weapon, the STR build opponent can just equip a similar speed weapon and always come out on top in the trade and never be staggered?  And also the fact STR builds generally means better shields which in turn means better against stamina loss on block and safe turtling unless you went 30 INT+30 FAITH with Chaos or Dark infused Great Corvian Scythe just to hard counter shields with chip damage.  At least DS2 had poise health and also a separate stat just for Weight which required additional investment if you actually wanted poise in your build. And DS3 also had weight as a separate stat requiring investment for poise, as well as poise being different and actually making sense balance-wise for weapons. Doesn't sit right with me that someone can poise through attacks with a little dagger or a straight sword.  But DS1 poise comboed with a single OP stat? PVP sounds like it's going to be bland and boring real fast.

This looks so good
So my big concern with Elden Ring actually is the artstyle. I'm replaying DS3 right now (for reasons completely unrelated to Elden Ring), and one of the things that's really struck me is the sheer spectacle of many of the zones. I especially remember Archdragon Peak, the Kiln of the First Flame, and Lothric as seen from the Firelink Shrine tower. With the last one especially, looking out at Lothric Castle, if you start from the bottom, you really start to get the sense of *why* it's called the High Wall of Lothric. Then you look down, and you realize how far it is from the top of the sheer cliffs the wall rests on to the ocean void below. Then you look *up*, and you see that all of that cliff and all of that wall isn't even halfway to the top of the castle keep.   DS3 was a true culmination, and the sheer scale and majesty of many of the areas really helped drive that home. And I kind of worry that Elden Ring won't be able to hit the same visual highs, which would be a terrible waste of its exploration mechanics. I can't think of anything better than parkouring all around the High Wall.

Not that I agree, I think the game is just beautiful from what I've been able to see so far, but I think people are complaining about the graphics because the Demon's Souls remake got a graphical overhaul from the original. Though that game looks beautiful as well, I think people are forgetting that open world games usually have to make sacrifices due to how much is usually loaded in at one time. The souls series had traditionally been a semi-linear experience with the illusion of open-world level design and this is the first time that they've tried actual open world design. I personally think people need to get over themselves when it comes to graphics (I've read some of the comments on that and some of them are saying that they won't play the game because of it), as gameplay and how the game runs are just as important... also, I say again, the game is beautiful and I really don't understand why people want "more" out of how it currently looks.  As far as I can tell, nothing looks jank and the textures are just fine.  (Ending Note: I've actually seen a lot about "graphics snobs" in recent years. People who won't play certain great games, just because the graphics aren't up to snuff in their opinion. I am fine with people wanting to play game for certain reasons and I can get behind aesthetic appeal being at least ONE reason why people play games, but they are severely limiting themselves with this kind of mentality. What I can't forgive however, are those people who say the game is actually bad just because the visuals aren't that great. A lot of indie titles would fall under that umbrella and among them there are great gems just waiting to be dug up! ^_^)

0:13 CRAB RAVE
Love Dark Souls and From Soft games, but honestly, I have no sympathy for invaders, too many people use invading as a way to grief players, spamming invasions an basically harassing people who are just trying to play through the game.I understand invasions are a part of the game to a point, but when the same person invades you for the 4th time in an area it really gets annoying, and then there are the hacker, those who invade with hacks on and are unable to be killed, have unlimited stamina, FP, and Items, or can cast 12 spells with 1 cast at teh same time, or strait up cause your player character to be stun locked by and unseen attack that prevents you from being able to do anything but log out of the game. This kind of stuff still happens in dark souls 3 and will most likely happen in elden ring, I know there are mods like Blue Sentinel to help mitigate cheaters but even that doesn't work 100% of the time, invasions in an area should be opt in and opt out, or at least time limited, in DS3 an invader has no time limit, so they can hide behind mobs all day, mean while your only counter to them doing that is 3  consumable items them lasts 30second each, and even if you do manage to use the seeds to kill an invader, they just re invade at no cost, and now you have 1 less seed to use, this is not a balanced system. Up the reward for successful invasions but give the players who are being invaded that advantages, invaders get 10 min maybe 20 in Elden ring since large area, players have a reusable item that has a small cooldown that makes invaders target able by NPC mobs for 1 min, and they can't connect to the same player for 30 min on success or failure. None of these things are game breaking, its a way of balancing the invasions, without a time limit an invader can just sit back and wait till the can get that once lucky bow shot while you are dealing with other mobs all day long, a time limit forces them to be aggressive and since they are invading you, I feel like that should be their prerogative. 30 seconds on a limited use item is absurd, at 40 stamina in DS3 you can practically dodge roll for 30 seconds strait, so this is the bare minimum of threat to an invader unless they are invading AFK and spawn next to a large number of enemies, or in areas with larger threats like the ghost archers in the ringed city. So a reusable item, with a cooldown so they can't spam it, and a longer effect so NPC mobs are more of a threat. The 30 min lock out between invasions to the same person is as I said to prevent people from harassing the same person or group of people over and over, in Dark Souls 3 I have been invaded by the same person in the same area and new areas multiple times, I think the most was 8 times in one zone, this just gets irritating and feel like a bit of harassment, there are plenty of people playing, you shouldn't only be dealing one 1 person or group for hours on end.

One thing that really impresses is how fluid and smooth the animations are. The Souls games are kinda known for having slightly choppy and jarring animations, especially when it comes to ripostes and things like that, and it's quite nice to see how organic everything looks. There's no snap to perform a riposte right where the animation is supposed to go like there is in the previous games, and movement looks so fluid like it is in the Witcher 3 or RDR2 rather than the clunky 8-axis movement animations you'll see in Dark Souls. Even when it comes to combat animations and attacking everything is so refined and smooth, it's crazy!

I like Dark Souls 2 a lot more than a good deal of From fans, but I was never that impressed with power stancing and I still don't see the big deal. In Dark Souls 2 it was just a few (very few) different attack animations that didn't actually add any additional layer of tactics or strategy. Like it was cool, I guess, but it seems like people have this idea in their head of it being the BEST THING when it was really just an underdeveloped mechanic that ultimately did not add much - I think the weapon arts from Dark Souls 3 ultimately add quite a bit more even if it wasn't as good a system as it could have been. All this praise I hear for power stancing feels like nostalgia goggles to me, or just people loving the idea of dual-wielding weapons having their own attacks, even if it's kinda half-baked. Hopefully Elden Ring makes it a bit more substantial. Not due to difficulty but that I found it dull both story and combat wise with it feeling too clich√© Japanese in places. Controversial I know. That being said it's disappointing to see a series of games that started out with rejections of modern AAA game design fully embrace it and become just like every other open-world action RPG. Nothing in ER looks like it's taking the kind of risks that Demon's Souls did, and a lot of what I hear about the design (boring bandit camps to clear out, fast travel from everywhere, little lights telling you where to go, giant beams of light in the world, Skyrim compass, Ubisoft towers, next to no fall damage) just doesn't sound good to me. It suggests they gave up on proper level design because they know that it'd be frustrating to explore their world without fast travel, so they just gave up and let you avoid the hassle of a journey entirely.

I honestly am not a big fan of how strength increases equip load instead of a dedicated stat, especially with how poise is going back to 1, where every weapon wants heavy armor. This will dramatically reduce build variety, making every dex build effectively a quality build. I understand that strength builds obviously need lots more equip load, but due to how every weapon class would REALLY want this poise, strength is just going to be leveled by most every build. I think Endurance would make the most sense, since strength builds also have lots of levels put into endurance due to the high stamina cost of many weapons, and endurance is already a useful stat to most builds, though perhaps endurance would be a bit OP like that. I also think a system like DS2 would be a better idea, to make some of the extremely large weapons more viable and useable on a meta level, as even in DS3 where they have a big advantage of actual poise on attacks, they still often fall flat compared to most fast weapons.

I know that people have memed a lot about Elden ring because it's taken so long to come out. However GOD DAM it looks worth it. I would happily have a company take their time like Fromsoft than deliver a broken uninspired game. Yes there is most likely going to be a few bugs or things that need adjusting but I would rather wait a few years/months for a better product than taking the alpha route which breaks your immersion as everything breaks. I have no problem with games that state they are alphas/beta builds but AAA devs have gotten quite lazy and just fix things way too late. The game looks stunning and feels nostalgia because you can feel the dark souls inspiration and yet it's own game with unique mechanics and being open world is quite a large leap for them to take but it makes you appreciate the amount of the work the level designer's had to do. Also I can already feel all the amazing mods that are going to come out for this game so we'll be playing this game for years to come. God bless you Fromsoft.

A new game for my Steam wishlist
I was uncertain about the open world, as frankly, I'm getting sick of them.  Open worlds were liberating and fresh coming off of 30 years of heavily constricted and controlled games, by now though they're getting long-in-the-tooth and no longer inherently provide any benefit IMO. Doesn't mean good open world games aren't out there, it's just being open world isn't much of a draw by itself anymore and often times, for devs who think it still is, leads to really dull games.  Hopefully Elden Ring is one of the good ones, and not one of the Ubisoft ones. >__>
The thing that's deterring me the most from this game is how it doesn't look to treat you with absolute contempt the way Dark Souls does. The powers the player gets, in particular, look very powerful. Maybe I'm being unfair though. The more I compare it to Dark Souls, the more frustrated I feel with it.
